    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app',

She fled from his damaged, drained life, and damaged and drained it even more. He doesn't just want her. He needs her. <br /><br /><b>lost.</b> <br />Isabel is trying to build herself a life in Los Angeles. It's not really working. She can play the game as well as all the other fakes...but what's the point? What is there to win?<br /><br /><b>sinner.</b><br />Cole and Isabel share a past that never seemed to have a future. They have the power to save each other and the power to tear each other apart. The only thing for certain is that they cannot let go.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4074141022285024107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2889617140" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13100177714901616180">3.5 stars<blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567305738i/28081714._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <i>“It sure is ugly.”<br/>“Ugly, never hurt a thing.” <br/>I scoffed. “Oh, ugly has hurt some things. It’s just that pretty hurts more.” </i>
</blockquote><b>Oof. Pseudo-philosophical YA at its<i> finest.</i></b><br/><br/>To catch everyone up -<b> Grace and Sam</b> (the main characters from the original series) are being their lovey-dovey selves back in Mercy Falls. <br/><br/><b>Isabelle and Cole </b>- the greatest couple that never-was - is not doing quite as well. <blockquote>
  <i>“Why did you even come here, Cole?”<br/>I touched her chin. This place, this beautiful p</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText13100177714901616180" style="display:none">3.5 stars<blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567305738i/28081714._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>“It sure is ugly.”<br>“Ugly, never hurt a thing.” <br>I scoffed. “Oh, ugly has hurt some things. It’s just that pretty hurts more.” </i>
</blockquote><b>Oof. Pseudo-philosophical YA at its<i> finest.</i></b><br><br>To catch everyone up -<b> Grace and Sam</b> (the main characters from the original series) are being their lovey-dovey selves back in Mercy Falls. <br><br><b>Isabelle and Cole </b>- the greatest couple that never-was - is not doing quite as well. <blockquote>
  <i>“Why did you even come here, Cole?”<br>I touched her chin. This place, this beautiful place, this girl, this beautiful girl, this music, this life. “I came here for you.” </i>
</blockquote>Isabelle is shipped off California in the wake of her parent's crumbling marriage.<br><br><b>Cole St. Clair trails after her</b>, allegedly to rekindle his rockstar career but truly to win Isabelle's heart.<blockquote>
  <i>It was the first time I'd really realized I'd lost my soul and that the beauty of not having a soul was that you couldn't seem to care that you no longer had one.</i>
</blockquote><b>Will he win back his lady-love? <i>Or will he lose himself in the process?</i></b><br><br>Man oh man. <br><br> Cole's shoulders must be<b>
  <i> aching </i>
</b>from carrying this book!<br><br>The werewolf rockstar reality TV premise was...surprisingly enjoyable. <br><br>I went in totally expecting to hate the plot (I mean...really...werewolf rockstar TV show???) but <b>it worked so effing well.</b><br><br>I (surprisingly) enjoyed the perspective of the Cole but Isabelle? Oof. <b> She was a soggy taco. </b><br><br>Oh good lawd. Someone please. Tell her there's more to life than <b>moping &amp; pouting</b> (oh sorry, I meant seeming perfectly totally cool and uncaring with everything).<br><br>Every time we swapped to her perspective, the little voice in the back of my head was like, "Whine, whine, whine. Anything new? More whining? Fab. Just. Fab."<br><br>I think that if she was like that for the first quarter to the first third, I would have been okay with it. But unfortuntely, she was like that until the last couple of pages, so we don't see much character growth.<br><br>Just her complaining about how her<b> rich little life was so <i>terrible,</i></b> how falling in love ruined her and how her family is absolutely terrible.<br><br>It's like...yes. I get that your parents are going through the divorce but the amount of angst we saw did not equate. <br><br>You'd think her best friend cheated with her dad given the amount of carrying-on Isabelle had (they didn't, for the record) (it was just a hella-lot of drama).<br><br>Sometimes seeing things from other characters' perspectives really rounds out the book... and sometimes not... very much not. <br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13100177714901616180" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_716379865" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/716379865" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/716379865?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

          marked it as on-hold




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=pn-shapeshifters">pn-shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2014-publication">2014-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=july">july</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=scholastic">scholastic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=own-dtb-tbr">own-dtb-tbr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer716379865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15586522504410213538">I am still in the camp that thinks <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6068551.Shiver__The_Wolves_of_Mercy_Falls___1_' title='Shiver (The Wolves of Mercy Falls, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shiver</a> would have been better as a standalone novel, but I find Maggie irresistible. So of course I'll read this...cautiously.</span>
  <span id="freeText15586522504410213538" style="display:none">I am still in the camp that thinks <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6068551.Shiver__The_Wolves_of_Mercy_Falls___1_" title="Shiver (The Wolves of Mercy Falls, #1) by Maggie Stiefvater" rel="nofollow noopener">Shiver</a> would have been better as a standalone novel, but I find Maggie irresistible. <div id="review_716370040" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/716370040" />
    <a title="Jessica (Step Into Fiction)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4986812-jessica-step-into-fiction"><img alt="Jessica (Step Into Fiction)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468260636p2/4986812.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/716370040?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica (Step Into Fiction)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica (Step Into Fiction)" href="/user/show/4986812-jessica-step-into-fiction">Jessica (Step Into Fiction)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4986812-jessica-step-into-fiction?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4986812-jessica-step-into-fiction?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4986812-jessica-step-into-fiction?shelf=autographed">autographed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer716370040" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12019365483212658979"><b>COLE!!!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/570826.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>My day has been made. <br/><br/>Now, to wait...<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380436186i/881545._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Review originally posted at <a href='http://www.stepintofiction.com/2014/07/sinner-by-maggie-stiefvater-review.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Step Into Fiction</a></b><br/><br/><u>Actual rating: 4.5 stars</u><br/><br/>I fangirled so hard when she first announced this book. The reason I kept reading the Shiver books was because of Cole and Isabel. No lie. He is one of my favorite male YA characters and for him to get his own book? Oh man, I was literally counting down the days. When I got my copy, I may have hugged it (actually, I did, I won't lie). But the big question is, did it live up to my expe</span>
  <span id="freeText12019365483212658979" style="display:none"><b>COLE!!!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/570826.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My day has been made. <br><br>Now, to wait...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380436186i/881545._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Review originally posted at <a href="http://www.stepintofiction.com/2014/07/sinner-by-maggie-stiefvater-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Step Into Fiction</a></b><br><br><u>Actual rating: 4.5 stars</u><br><br>I fangirled so hard when she first announced this book. The reason I kept reading the Shiver books was because of Cole and Isabel. No lie. He is one of my favorite male YA characters and for him to get his own book? Oh man, I was literally counting down the days. When I got my copy, I may have hugged it (actually, I did, I won't lie). But the big question is, did it live up to my expectations? Yes . . . and no.<br><br>We'll start with the no part first, shall we? I was expecting more paranormal but what I got was more contemporary. Not necessarily a bad thing except when you're a person like me who isn't the biggest fan of YA contemp. However, I said I didn't care because I mean, hello! It's Cole St. Clair and Isabel Culpeper. But really, this was my only negative thing about this book. I'd say that's a pretty good thing, right?<br><br>On to the good. COLE. Okay, so we got to be in his head in both Linger and Forever but having an entire book (okay, really more like half since it's split with Isabel but you get my point) from him and about him? Oh yeah, I'm all over that. I may not have loved the Wolves of Mercy Falls series, as Sam and Grace bored to me death but I liked it enough that the chance to read more made me do the jig. The one thing I loved most but also frustrated me the most about this book was the fact that both Cole and Isabel were dealing with personal demons. Isabel frustrated me more than Cole did but I think that's because Cole has such a laid back personality that you just shrug it off. Let's be honest, Isabel has family issues. We came across these issues in the previous books but you really see a lot more in these books. Because of this, she doesn't believe in love and definitely doesn't believe in marriage but yet, she can't escape these feelings she has for Cole, again.<br><br>There are random appearances, per say, of both Sam and Grace so fans of the previous books will get a little excitement out of those. They're both short but I enjoyed having them in there. Cole makes friends with one of the most random guys in this book and you know what? It's one of the best parts about this book. You don't have to be a somebody for Cole to take notice of you, you just have to hold his interest enough to care. I want to meet someone like him in real life, I just feel like it would be an adventure in itself.<br><br>For those who love romance and kissing, let me just say you will not be disappointed. There is so much kissing and Cole's version of romancing that it made me giddy reading it.<br><br>If you liked the Wolves of Mercy Falls series and especially if you're like me and a big fan of Cole, this is something you don't want to miss out on. However, if you haven't read the series, I feel like this could be read on it's own and you'd enjoy just the same. There's references to things that happened in the previous books but they tell you enough about what's happened that I don't think you'd be lost.<br><br>Thank you so much to Scholastic for allowing us the opportunity to get this book at BEA in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12019365483212658979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_716563246" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/716563246" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/716563246?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=best-of-2014">best-of-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer716563246" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17561708096069081201"><b>[read 2 | Oct 2020]</b><br/>Softly crying that it's been 6 years since I read this book and with the way my memory is, it was practically like being gifted the treasure of a whole new Stiefvater book. 😭 I adored this reread, this angry and chaotic and apocalyptic and emotional collision of what it means to be alive. Again, it delves so deeply into depression and suicidal thoughts, and I thought it handled it with such nuance. Cole also, and I cannot be persuaded against this, has adhd. He is such a textb</span>
  <span id="freeText17561708096069081201" style="display:none"><b>[read 2 | Oct 2020]</b><br />Softly crying that it's been 6 years since I read this book and with the way my memory is, it was practically like being gifted the treasure of a whole new Stiefvater book. 😭 I adored this reread, this angry and chaotic and apocalyptic and emotional collision of what it means to be alive. Again, it delves so deeply into depression and suicidal thoughts, and I thought it handled it with such nuance. Cole also, and I cannot be persuaded against this, has adhd. He is such a textbook case smh. I love him. I love spying neurodiversities in the wild and wondering if it was intentional or not. And Isabel's ice-queen sharpness, her bitter loneliness, her way of living with every wall raised to cope with trauma...I cry for her. She wasn't easy to love and Cole wasn't easy to tolerate. Their contrast, their catastrophic collisions. The <i>best</i>.<br /><br />My only retrospective disappointments were I thought Isabel needed a more solid ending...her arc felt rushed (especially the finale scene didn't feel like her?) whereas Cole's landed most excellently. And there are a few micoragressions which are never alright.<br /><br />Also <b>the audiobook is gorgeous.</b> Incredible narrators and highly recommend!<br /><br /><br /><b>[read 1 | July 2014]</b><br /><b>You know I'm a fan of Maggie Stiefvater. </b> So I. freaked. out when I got a copy and I promptly dropped everything and read it. In one day. And I just...how do I review it? How do I even function?<br />There some books that remind you why you're absolutely obsessed with stories. This is one of them.<br /><br />Maggie Stiefvater wrote this trilogy called <i>The Wolves of Mercy Falls</i> which includes Shiver, Linger, and Forever. They start off narrated by Grace, who is obsessed with wolves (which are actually werewolves because it's a bit weird to fall in love with an animal...so we fall in love with half-animals-half-humans). Gradually more squalling people/animals enter the picture. Sam is Grace's One True Love. He's a wolf. Then enters Cole: also a wolf. And Isabel: not a wolf, but as frosty as machete in Antarctica.<br /><br />Sam and Grace are art and muse. Cole and Isabel are knife and fire.<br /><br />I happen to love them a lot, maybe not <i>more</i> than Sam/Grace, but it's so equal my capacity for intense adoration is exhausting me. When I heard there'd be a standalone about Cole and Isabel in the What Happened After Shiverlingerforever Ended -- I knew I would love it.<br /><br /><b> It's also about music. </b> Don't underestimate how freakishly hard it is to write a musical book. Musical movies are fine. You have ears. Musical books must sing you the music using mere words. How hard is that? Sinner, of course, pulls it off with flying colours and crackling chords. I adore music and I love that I could hear and feel it while reading the book.<br /><br /><b> And can we just talk about how good the writing is? </b> It's huge on the visuals, smells and feels details. 5-senses! Who'd have thought they could change a book from "cool" to "freakishly awesome"? I absolutely love how closely I could experience the book. The description isn't flooding over page after page. It uses punchy words. Then it's done.<br /><i><br /> The McMansion was sterile enough to actually remove pieces of my identity every time I returned to it, insidiously replacing them with wall-to-wall white carpet and blond hardwood floors.</i><br /><b>or</b><br /><i>I felt a not entirely great sensation in my stomach, like someone was opening an umbrella inside it. </i><br /><br />A few words and -- BOOM -- the clearest picture is in your mind.<br /><br /><b>It's funny. (Did I mention I like funny?) </b> The banter between Cole and Isabel is the best because they are really mean people who act like they hate each other and couldn't care less -- when really they care so so much and they can't bear the thought of losing each other. Lo<br /><br /><b> There is a brief Sam and Grace cameo.</b> It's note enough, mind you. I was hoping they'd at least squeeze a scene in together.<br /><br /><b>I just love this book.</b> I couldn't put it down. It made me want to write a million things and read a million things and just appreciate the greatest art that is books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17561708096069081201" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_955498381" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/955498381" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/955498381?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer955498381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13955751890481022808">It has been a while since I read the Wolves of Mercy Falls series, so I was a bit worried that remembering next to no details about it would make reading this a flop, but it was not a problem at all. If you want to refresh your memory there's a convenient Wikipedia page that reminds you who's who. But everything you need to know is recapped (albeit briefly) as we go along. <br/><br/>Sinner is narrated by our beloved Cole and Isabel, a couple of characters who you won't soon forget. Cole is somewhat of an </span>
  <span id="freeText13955751890481022808" style="display:none">It has been a while since I read the Wolves of Mercy Falls series, so I was a bit worried that remembering next to no details about it would make reading this a flop, but it was not a problem at all. If you want to refresh your memory there's a convenient Wikipedia page that reminds you who's who. But everything you need to know is recapped (albeit briefly) as we go along. <br><br>Sinner is narrated by our beloved Cole and Isabel, a couple of characters who you won't soon forget. Cole is somewhat of an arrogant ass, yet charming and hilarious, and Isabel is a bit psychotic with quick wit and, to be honest, she scares me a little &gt;.&lt; I love her, though. She's sarcastic and may be cold at times, but she's just so real and gets that sometimes life just freaking sucks. Plus she doesn't take any shit from anybody and that's something I always respect. As for Cole, sometimes I love him, other times I just want to slap that smug face of his. He does take some patience, but you know that he really does mean well - especially when it comes to Isabelle. I also love how much he's changed, and even though the world seems to be against him he gives them the finger and keeps on keeping on. That's a true sign of strength if you ask me. Also I have to mention Leon - for a side character, he entertained! <br><br>Together… Cole and Isabel can definitely bring out the worst in each other. It's a complicated relationship, that's for sure. They have a lot of wounds to heal, and a lot of issues to work out. As expected, it's a hot and cold kind of romance, but for once I wasn't irritated by it. I completely understood why Isabel reacted the way she did, and her lack of trust is not hard to grasp - who expects a guy to <i>actually</i> have changed when his personality is such an extreme? Their chemistry is off the charts, though, and you can feel how much love they have for each other despite all the crap they went through. It makes it easy to root for them.<br><br>The plot, honestly there's not much paranormal going on in this book. It's a werewolf book, yes, but the werewolf is nothing but another burden Cole is trying to be rid of. We do see him turn occasionally, but this novel focuses more on its contemporary side. It's a story about a boy learning to live with the harsh consequences of his past choices. It's also a love story. It's slow-ish paced, but the characters and situations keep you compelled. Cole being semi-famous lends the book a dash of the "life of the rich and famous". He also takes on a reality show for an extra spin of drama as well. I was actually quite fascinated by it all. <br><br>In a dazzling, sometimes frustrating LA setting, Sinner is full of wonder, heartbreak, and colourful characters for a great addition to the original Wolves of Mercy Falls series. This one is less wolf, and more broken human, but fans of the series will love it nonetheless!<br><br>--<br><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for review.</i><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388702323i/7905232.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_857273669" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/857273669" />
    <a title="jv poore" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5157918-jv-poore"><img alt="jv poore" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570108420p2/5157918.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/857273669?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jv poore" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jv poore" href="/user/show/5157918-jv-poore">jv poore</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=buried-under-books">buried-under-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer857273669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6181830074983823355">While Sinner, the recently released, highly anticipated, companion book to the Shiver trilogy; didn’t take me back to Mercy Falls, it most certainly allowed me an enchanting opportunity to revisit Cole St. Clair and Isabel Culpepper. If you, like me, loved absolutely every single thing about the Shiver trilogy, my best guess is that you will revere Sinner. On the other hand, if this is the very first you’ve heard of said trilogy, I can still unabashedly recommend Sinner as a remarkable stand-alo</span>
  <span id="freeText6181830074983823355" style="display:none">While Sinner, the recently released, highly anticipated, companion book to the Shiver trilogy; didn’t take me back to Mercy Falls, it most certainly allowed me an enchanting opportunity to revisit Cole St. Clair and Isabel Culpepper. If you, like me, loved absolutely every single thing about the Shiver trilogy, my best guess is that you will revere Sinner. On the other hand, if this is the very first you’ve heard of said trilogy, I can still unabashedly recommend Sinner as a remarkable stand-alone novel packed with the punch that only Ms. Stiefvater can deliver. Even if you are “not really into the whole werewolf thing”, I stand by my recommendation. To me, the werewolf in Sinner is more an allegory than a creature to be feared or envied. <br /><br />Ms. Stiefvater’s newest novel is a fast-paced, engrossing read that ebbs and flows with generosity and narcissism, love and hate, determined clinging and letting go. There is love and laughter, heart-ache and tears, mistakes, self-realizations and forgiveness. It is about life, growing up, being true, acting brave and accepting that; sometimes, walking away isn’t a cowardly act; but rather, the hardest and most definite thing you will ever have to do. Lessons generally learned much later in life become imperative in the formation and revelation of the true self as both Cole and Isabel; separately, yet simultaneously, become a bit more open and a little less jaded. Not embracing, but almost acknowledging that options aside from black or white, wrong or right, indeed exist. Grey comes in many shades, the road less traveled still delivers the traveler to his destination; and sometimes, pausing to ponder “what’s the way?” is the only way to keep going forward.<br /><br />As always, within a Stiefvater saga, there are serendipitous seeds of wisdom that, when nurtured, bloom with breath-taking splendor. The brief glimpse of family on the beach is beautifully brilliant, encapsulating both a smiley and a teary moment (this author is a sneaky, clever, creator). If you’ve read this book, but weren’t captivated, amused and delighted….you may not have been paying close attention.<br /><br />Leon. Leon’s pictures. The insightful inclusion of this quiet, soft-spoken man adds depth and a certain melancholy, elevating the book to a new level. <br /><br />Sofia, because every darkness deserves a ray of light; and every home, a little hope.<br /><br />I closed Forever four years ago with mixed emotions and a heavy heart. I had fallen for these characters, accepted the finality; but longed for just a little bit more Cole and Isabel. The two characters are so vibrant; filled with energy, anger, frustration, confusion, yet appearing confident and collected. They required their very own story and Sinner is it, spot on.<br /><br /> This review was written for Buried Under Books Blog.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6181830074983823355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5308912556763209093" style="display:none"><b>Sinner (The Wolves of Mercy Falls, #4), Maggie Stiefvater</b><br /><br />I loved all of the four novels of this series, in the <b>Sinner</b>, Cole travels to Los Angeles, California and visits Isabel, persuading her to agree to have dinner with him. The discovery that Cole did not come to California to find her, but instead to return to the spot light, devastates Isabel. She refuses to be on the show, calling Cole to accuse him of lying to her, before telling him to drop dead.<br /><br />Cole begins living in the house supplied by Baby alongside the three-member band she had arranged. Cameras are sewn throughout the house, with a camera crew to match. After rejecting the guitarist and bassist chosen for him, he decidedly informs Baby's that he shall conduct the auditions himself. <span id="freeTextContainer15477779253616202231"><i>July 28, 2014<br/>Oh, God, it was exhausting! If I get over the urge to kill myself, maybe I'll write a review.</i><br/><br/><i>July 31, 2014</i><br/>So now that I managed to pull myself together, I have to say this book was a huge disappointment. I loved Cole and Isabel’s blooming romance in Forever, and waited for this book so much. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406721793i/10588506._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Cole.</b> He is still captivating: he has humor, improvement, can see the people and things around him. He is very sensitive to everything, and could morph everything into something phenomenal – eve</span>
  <span id="freeText15477779253616202231" style="display:none"><i>July 28, 2014<br>Oh, God, it was exhausting! If I get over the urge to kill myself, maybe I'll write a review.</i><br><br><i>July 31, 2014</i><br>So now that I managed to pull myself together, I have to say this book was a huge disappointment. I loved Cole and Isabel’s blooming romance in Forever, and waited for this book so much. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406721793i/10588506._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Cole.</b> He is still captivating: he has humor, improvement, can see the people and things around him. He is very sensitive to everything, and could morph everything into something phenomenal – even bad phenomenal, but still phenomenal. He is able to build something valuable even from shit. <br><blockquote>
  <i>Things come in my eyes and ears and through my pores, and my receptors begin to pulse restlessly and my neurons fire like cannons, and by the time everything gets into my brain and comes out the other side, it’s all transformed into a different species, pixels or channels, glossy or matt. I can’t change the way I’m made. I’m a performer, a singer, a werewolf, a sinner.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>Isabel</b> is poisonous. She squeezes all the happiness and joy out of everyone around her. She is always angry, always rude, bored and bitter. She hates everyone: her parents, her colleagues, everyone she knows and everyone she doesn’t even know.<br><br><i>"The place was already full of people. God, I hated them all."</i><br><br>Lovely. Who wouldn’t want to be with this girl?<br><br>Both Isabel and Cole think in extremes. Isabel is immature, aggressive and hysterical, Cole is pseudo-suicidal. While there is development in Cole’s character, there is nothing in Isabel’s. Cole has a purpose: it is Isabel. He subordinates everything to this aim. His every thought is about Isabel. And Isabel, being absolutely self-obsessed, is blind to it. <br><blockquote>
  <i>I had told the truth, and it hadn’t mattered. In the end, she’d bought into the same story everyone else had. Did it matter if you’d changed if no one believed it?</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406721793i/10588507._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The story.</b> The reality show left me uninterested. The paranormal aspect of the story is inconsistent, makes no sense, and reduced to almost zero. As if it doesn’t even exist. <br><br><b>Romance.</b> No development, no communication, no magic moments. After 60% of the story I just stopped caring about the characters. I didn’t even root for their happy ending. The happy ending is unexpected and unestablished. I still love Cole, and he’d deserve a much better story than this and a much better person than Isabel. <br><br><b>Secondary characters.</b> The only truly respectable and likeable person in this story is Leon, the Cadillac driver. Oh, and Jeremy! And Sofia. Baby, and the others are only papier mache figures. <br><br><b><i>Sinner</i> is sickeningly sad and depressive.</b> I could write that it is not for me - well, actually it's true - and that maybe you’d enjoy it - but that wouldn’t be true. So much fake angst, but no real drama. So read it at your own risk.<br><br><b>Two stars</b> because Cole has some affectionate moments, and because of Leon, Jeremy and Sofia. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1406721793i/10588508._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15477779253616202231" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14145162272500350941">This was me, starting the book↓<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409130781ra/10937737.gif' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Yes, I was a wriggly feline, unable to contain my excitement and anticipation and so decided to squirm under the couch; successfully managing to startle my fellow feline friend in the process.<br/><br/>Anyway, let me get back to <i>Sinner</i>, the marvelously marvellous book written by none other than one of my favourite authors, Maggie Stiefvater! The book surpassed my higher-than-Mt-Everest expectations and left me with that utterly satisfying feeling you get when you wake up an</span>
  <span id="freeText14145162272500350941" style="display:none">This was me, starting the book↓<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409130781ra/10937737.gif" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Yes, I was a wriggly feline, unable to contain my excitement and anticipation and so decided to squirm under the couch; successfully managing to startle my fellow feline friend in the process.<br><br>Anyway, let me get back to <i>Sinner</i>, the marvelously marvellous book written by none other than one of my favourite authors, Maggie Stiefvater! The book surpassed my higher-than-Mt-Everest expectations and left me with that utterly satisfying feeling you get when you wake up and realise that you still have more time to sleep.<br><br>Sinner was hilarious, sarcastic and genuine; an all-rounder book that had me grinning like the Cheshire Cat. Cole St. Clair is an indescribably brilliant character and it was mesmerizing to read from his perspective. His snark, humour, sarcasm and charm were dizzying and I have begun to memorize his countless one-liners and retorts that would leave you grasping for a comeback, or more likely, scratching your head. And all I have to say is- Cole St Clair...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1385014126ra/7044930.gif" width="400" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>And that's not all; no sir, there is still Isabel to gush over. Isabel's cynicism, scorn and temperament were magnetizing in their own way, and I found myself constantly smirking at her snide, witty remarks.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409130781ra/10937738.gif" width="400" height="310" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The side characters were very amusing and the writing style flawless. I would recommend this book not only to each and every fan of Maggie Stiefvater or/and the Shiver trilogy but also to anyone looking for a book that will make them melt into a puddle of emotions.<br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br>YES. This is sure to be AMAZING!<br><br>Can't wait. Cole, Cole, Cole and Cole is going to be <b>AWESOME!</b> Oh, wait- did I mention that Cole was going to be awesome? Well, let me say it again.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>Cole is going to be AWESOME!</u>
  </i>
</b> And Isabel too =)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380425216ra/848382.gif" width="400" height="280" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Looks like Taylor Swift is excited. <div id="review_716531510" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/716531510" />
    <a title="Glass" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4808910-glass"><img alt="Glass" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583244629p2/4808910.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/716531510?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Glass" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Glass" href="/user/show/4808910-glass">Glass</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20527160-sinner">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Glass by: </span>
      Buddy read with Tanja
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808910-glass?shelf=girls-reading-together">girls-reading-together</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808910-glass?shelf=tanja-zemira-miss-glass-book-club">tanja-zemira-miss-glass-book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808910-glass?shelf=fangirling-like-crazy">fangirling-like-crazy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer716531510" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer848496665036004794"><br/><b>Tanja:</b> You of all people know how much I love Maggie's writing and how I drive people crazy with it. So I can't help but wonder where did it go. I couldn't find it here, which makes me rather sad.<br/><b>Glass:</b> I was always raving about how amazing this woman writes, but I have to agree with you and say that I am rather disappointed with Cole's story. I expected epic conclusion, but left hanging dry. What happened?<br/><b>Tanja:</b> I have no idea where all the magic disappeared. But to organize our thoughts better</span>
  <span id="freeText848496665036004794" style="display:none"><br /><b>Tanja:</b> You of all people know how much I love Maggie's writing and how I drive people crazy with it. So I can't help but wonder where did it go. I couldn't find it here, which makes me rather sad.<br /><b>Glass:</b> I was always raving about how amazing this woman writes, but I have to agree with you and say that I am rather disappointed with Cole's story. I expected epic conclusion, but left hanging dry. What happened?<br /><b>Tanja:</b> I have no idea where all the magic disappeared. But to organize our thoughts better I propose we list pros and cons here. So would you like to start?<br /><b>Glass:</b> Perfect! Let's see...<br /><br /><u>
  <b>What we liked:</b>
</u><br /><br /><b>Glass:</b> I was so happy with how Maggie Stiefvater managed to avoid all stereotypes of genre and gave us a story which is this amazing crossover between young adult and new adult. I didn't expect anything else from a woman who wrote Scorpio Races.<br /><b>Tanja:</b> I totally agree with that. I also liked how Maggie kept this story apart from The Wolves of Mercy Falls. Sinner is set in LA which put both characters away from everything that happened before. You can read this story on its own, but at the same time I suggest you read the first series.<br /><b>Glass:</b> That is true, most of the companion novels are about same events but usually told from a point of view of a supporting character. Speaking about characters, that is one more plus - both Cole and Isabel are different than in previous novels. At moments I even wondered if I had missed something important between Forever and Sinner.<br /><b>Tanja:</b> I felt the same. My favorite thing or better said moment in this story was when Cole came to pick Isabel up after that party. I could feel bits of old Cole and Isabel then. But even though they did behave like before it was brought to the limit where I didn't enjoy it.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>What we didn't like:</b>
</u> <br /><br /><b>Tanja:</b> Like I said at the start there is the writing which was nothing like that poetic sort we had in the previous books. I missed it and my heard ached for it. But still my biggest problem was to determine the point of this story. I didn't see it then and I still cannot see it now.<br /><b>Glass:</b> Also, it had this really weird atmosphere - like a mix of Reckless by S.C. Stephens and Great Gatsby by Scott Fitzgerald. One second I love how she pulls me into Cole's head, it's like I am right there with him and everything he feels, I feel. But then comes this big eye-roll moment and it's like I'm reading completely different book.<br /><b>Tanja:</b> Yes, both characters were taken to their extreme and we could see that their relationship was too destructive. It wasn't balanced and that's why the ending itself felt a bit off for me. Everything happened so fast that at moment I though that was it, the next chapter things turned out of sudden. Drama, and hot and cold moments were too much and I didn't like it.<br /><b>Glass:</b> Well, I've read about more destructive relationships and you know that melodrama is my guilty pleasure, so I didn't have much issues with that. What did bother me is something I usually say for John Green's novels - pretentious writing and characters that try too hard to sound "witty" and "cool". And I can't believe that I am describing that way something Maggie Stiefvater wrote.<br /><br /><u>
  <b>In the end...</b>
</u><br /><br />We are not sorry for reading this book because it was wonderful to get back to our favorite series, but other than being enjoyable and quick read, Sinner was not what we expected. Fans of The Wolves of Mercy Falls might read it "just because", but in the end, we doubt that it will be a memorable read. <br /><br />Review posted at <a href="http://jacitamati.blogspot.com/2014/07/sinner-wolves-of-mercy-falls-35-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Ja čitam, a ti?</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="848496665036004794" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1426843743" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1426843743" />
    <a title="Lia  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48295288-lia"><img alt="Lia  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594824825p2/48295288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1426843743?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lia  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lia  " href="/user/show/48295288-lia">Lia  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=english-and-american-lit-and-more">english-and-american-lit-and-more</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=books-i-love">books-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=werewolves">werewolves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=amazing-characters-are-amazing">amazing-characters-are-amazing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=fictional-boyfriend">fictional-boyfriend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48295288-lia?shelf=main-character-is-on-point">main-character-is-on-point</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1426843743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15341054039741527470"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>We were so little, when you took away all our sins.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/><br/><br/>Going into a book, we all have certain expectations: <i>I'm going to like this, it's gonna be amazing, it's probably not my cup of tea...</i> - you know, that sort of thing. Going into this book, I never would've thought it was going to be a 5 stars book. I mean, it's a spin-off of a trilogy I read <i>years</i> ago, so I wasn't expecting it to be anything more than okay. Turns out I was wrong. But let me explain myself a little better.<br/><br/>I read The W</span>
  <span id="freeText15341054039741527470" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>We were so little, when you took away all our sins.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br /><br /><br />Going into a book, we all have certain expectations: <i>I'm going to like this, it's gonna be amazing, it's probably not my cup of tea...</i> - you know, that sort of thing. Going into this book, I never would've thought it was going to be a 5 stars book. I mean, it's a spin-off of a trilogy I read <i>years</i> ago, so I wasn't expecting it to be anything more than okay. Turns out I was wrong. But let me explain myself a little better.<br /><br />I read The Wolves of Mercy Falls trilogy as soon as it came out here in Italy, which was roughly four years ago. I know this is kind of an unpopular opinion, because a lot of people seem not to have liked it, but I loved it: I don't know if I would like it just as much if I read it today but, honestly?, I think I would. Not only this trilogy made me fall further in love with the fantasy genre, but it made me even more determined to be a writer. I was absolutely amazed by Maggie Stiefvater's writing and Sam, one of the two MCs of the trilogy, will always be one of my favorite characters ever. But the thing I loved the most about The Wolves of Mercy Falls was not the writing, or even the great characters, but how it made me feel. Which is exactly how Sinner made me feel.<br />It's the most pleasant of unpleasant feelings. It's like when you're with a lot of people and you've been talking and laughing for hours and they seem to think you're nice and funny, and then you suddenly realize that this isn't you. It's all an act, and they're all buying it, and what else can you do? You keep going. You get that cold feeling on your skin and that emptiness in your throat, and you keep giving them what they want, even though you know you're a fraud. This is how Sinner made me feel. Like I was stripped bare of all my secrets, and I had no choice but to look straight at the truth.<br /><br />Cole St. Clair is a former rockstar, former drug addict and werewolf. Everyone thought him dead, and then suddenly he was not. His mind is a dangerous place. It's sweet and sour and intoxicating like rotten fruit. He keeps making the same mistakes and going round and round and he can't help it, because he's an addict - and this is exactly what people with addictive personalities do. They do not care for self-destruction and they do not care for themselves. They just stay still and watch as their own body and mind slowly turn to ashes. Cole is not sad and he doesn't feel sorry for himself: he's desperate, but in a way that burns. He can be euphoric one moment and depressed the next, and everything he does and says it's always too much. He turns <i>all the fire inside</i> so he won't hurt anyone else, and his soul burns instead. He's a different person now, not the one he used to be, but the truth is... you can only change so much. He knows loss and he knows love, and there is nothing more beautiful than the desperate and all-consuming way he loves Isabel.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"Death is not morbid" he said "Everything else is."</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Isabel Culpeper has got an heart of steel. She's lost her brother, and her family is slowly falling apart, so her only choice is to put on a mask and act completely indifferent to the whole world. While Cole is burning, she is slowly fading. She treats people with cold sarcasm and never has a kind word for anyone, not even for her shy and awkward cousin Sofia, and certainly not for her parents. Isabel's family is a broken one. She tries to be icy-cold and not to fall in love with Cole all over again and to be immune to the storm she's found herself into, and sometimes she even tries to lose herself in a world she doesn't quite understand, but it never works. Isabel is not <i>everyone else</i>. While the world sees her as a cold soul, she's burning with anger. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"I feel like I'm the only sane person in the world. I don't get why this whole world runs on stupidity."</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><br />This was not an easy book for me. Sometimes it hit a little too close to home and it told me things I didn't want to know, it reminded me of things I didn't want to remember, but this is exactly why I love this trilogy. Because unlike anything else I've ever read, it gives me the sweet feeling of decay, of life and death, of everything broken that maybe - only maybe - can be fixed. <br />Now I really want to reread the entire trilogy, even though I should definitely get new copies. I have the Italian edition of all three books and not only I want to read them in English, but my editions also have the ugliest covers you could ever think of. Thank you very much, Italian publishers. So yeah, joyfully ignoring the fact that I'm penniless, I'm officially getting new copies of The Wolves of Mercy Falls trilogy! And of course, I'm getting a copy of Sinner as well, because if you didn't already get that impression from my review... it was pretty fucking awesome. <br /><br /><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>We are a wonder of checks and balances to keep on running. The human body doesn't want to get hurt. There was something wrong with me, because sometimes I didn't care. There was something wrong with me, because sometimes I wanted it. We fear death; we fear the void; we scrabble to keep our pulses. I was the void.</blockquote>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15341054039741527470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_879346573" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/879346573" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/879346573?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer879346573" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15134570846736794682"><b>2.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>I have very mixed feelings about <b>Sinner</b>. There were parts I loved: the writing and the chemistry between Cole and Isabel, and then there was the not so much. I will say I was happy to have closure for Cole and Isabel after so long.<br/><br/>Cole has moved to Los Angeles in an attempt to re-start his music career. But the main reason he chose L.A. is because Isabel is there and Cole wants a future with her. Instead of signing on with a record label Cole has agreed to make an album while having it </span>
  <span id="freeText15134570846736794682" style="display:none"><b>2.5 Stars</b><br /><br />I have very mixed feelings about <b>Sinner</b>. There were parts I loved: the writing and the chemistry between Cole and Isabel, and then there was the not so much. I will say I was happy to have closure for Cole and Isabel after so long.<br /><br />Cole has moved to Los Angeles in an attempt to re-start his music career. But the main reason he chose L.A. is because Isabel is there and Cole wants a future with her. Instead of signing on with a record label Cole has agreed to make an album while having it documented by a “reality” show. One that specializes in featuring stars self-destruct in the process. Cole finds Isabel and inside she dares to dream that he’s here just for her. In Cole’s mind he is, but when Isabel finds out about the “reality” show she’s ticked and rightfully so in my opinion. What sane girl relishes the idea of her potential boyfriend/partner staring in a reality show? I get hives just thinking about it! <br /><br />Sinner had a couple of things going against it (for me) from the beginning that may not be a problem for other readers. First of all, the whole premise of starring in a sensationalized reality show was a big negative for me. I can’t stand “reality” shows that are high on drama and character implosions. Second, even though I live in a suburb of Los Angeles, I hate the fake and superficial Los Angeles/Hollywood lifestyle where everyone must have the newest, brightest, best of everything: looks and things. And this is the setting. Cole and Isabel didn’t buy into that, but still, that was the setting and it came through loud and clear. I think this is the main reason it felt so different from the rest of the Wolves of Mercy Falls series. It didn’t feel anything like it, actually. The whole shifting and wolf thing hardly factored in the story at all. <br /><br />The chemistry between Cole and Isabel was palpable and they shared some very sexy moments. It was the best thing about the story, IMO. But, this was not a couple gradually rejoining, sharing life’s burdens and bonding over common feelings. There was no such “togetherness”. Cole and Isabel had their own problems they didn’t really discuss with each other. Each dealt separately and then they’d come together here and there and smooch. Granted, these smooch-fests were very lusty, Maggie is a whiz at building the moment up, but I want more than just kissing. I want a deep connection, but Cole and Isabel were never really on the same page for the better part of the book. Cole was always chasing and Isabel was always running. That was okay, it was nothing unbearable because, like I said they’d get together and have these amazing moments, but then the last 20% there was a series of strange and unhappy events. I wouldn’t say it was high drama, just more melancholy angstiness, and then BAM at the very end everything is settled without really sorting anything out. I was a little bewildered, and I’m still scratching my head to be honest. <br /><br />I do adore Maggie’s writing and I’m always in awe at how she’s able to set the mood and make you feel every scene as though it were happening to you, but I was hoping for more. Especially since Cole and Isabel were my favorite couple in Forever. <br /><i><br />A copy was provided by the publisher in exchange for a honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15134570846736794682" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_771276994" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/771276994" />
    <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously"><img alt="Rachel Reads Ravenously" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539149211p2/14514998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/771276994?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Reads Ravenously" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=werewolves-shapeshifters">werewolves-shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=hardcover">hardcover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer771276994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2629719239072345290"><b> 4.5 Sinner stars </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “I came back for you, Isabel.” </i> </b><br/><br/><a href='http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/sinner.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404962974i/10314242.png' alt=' photo sinner.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Sinner is the follow up to Maggie Stiefvater’s Wolves of Mercy Falls trilogy, and in order to understand this book completely, you must read those three amazing books first.<br/><br/>After the events of Forever, Isabel has moved from Minnesota to Los Angeles with her mother, moved in with her cousin and is pursuing a career in medicine. Cole, the haunted musician turned werewolf, has followed her back to the city that played a part in his downfall. B</span>
  <span id="freeText2629719239072345290" style="display:none"><b> 4.5 Sinner stars </b><br><br><b> <i> “I came back for you, Isabel.” </i> </b><br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/sinner.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404962974i/10314242.png" alt=" photo sinner.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Sinner is the follow up to Maggie Stiefvater’s Wolves of Mercy Falls trilogy, and in order to understand this book completely, you must read those three amazing books first.<br><br>After the events of Forever, Isabel has moved from Minnesota to Los Angeles with her mother, moved in with her cousin and is pursuing a career in medicine. Cole, the haunted musician turned werewolf, has followed her back to the city that played a part in his downfall. Both Isabel and Cole are trying to move on from their past and become better versions of themselves, but are they standing in their own way?<br><br><b> <i> “Did it matter if you changed if no one believed it?” </i> </b><br><br>This book was eloquently written and pretty much everything I wanted in a follow up book about my favorite characters. In this book Isabel is still trying to recover from the death of her brother and the destruction of her family. Isabel is constantly hiding behind her anger and harsh words, but she’s only doing this to hide the fact that she feels too much. Isabel also fears that she’ll fall in love with Cole again, and that when she did, he would break her.<br><br><b> <i> “I had been taken apart and put back together again, and this version of me was unbreakable.” </i> </b><br><br>Cole finds himself reverting back into the life of a rockstar, starring in a unique new reality show and recording a new album. In place of drugs, Cole has used transforming into the wolf as a way to stop feeling, heroine for werewolfism. Isabel is the only person who understands Cole for who he really is. Cole doesn’t need to hide behind his persona when he’s around her, he can be his true self. Their connection comes from the fact that they both see each other for who they really are, and not what other people see them as.<br><br><b> <i> “Why did you come back?”<br>“I came back because I had to. Because there was nothing wrong in the world except that I was getting older in it.” </i> </b><br><br>Cole swears to Isabel that he came to LA just for her, but Isabel is not a fan of seeing Cole fall back into his old life. For Cole, coming back to LA means facing his demons, and the city can either help him move on, or it could take away the last part of his soul.<br><br><b> <i> “I knew just how it felt when your worst fear was that you would be yourself.” </i> </b><br><br> Los Angeles is a huge theme in this book, signifying rebirth and redemption for both of the main characters. I had fun reading this, being a resident of the greater Los Angeles area, because I could tell that the author either did her research, or has spent a lot of time in Los Angeles and has a key appreciation of it. Los Angeles was not glorified, and it was not criticized, it just was in this book.<br><br>The romantic plot was actually the majority of this book. It’s been a while since I read the trilogy before it, but I didn’t remember that much of a focus on romance. Not that I minded, as I said Cole and Isabel are my favorite, so it was a nice change to see Cole just got for it and to try and get Isabel. His determination and devotion to her showed how much he had really changed from his past life. <br><br><b> <i> “Tell me you’ll see me tomorrow.”<br>“I’ll see you tomorrow.”<br>“Tell me you’ll see me the next day. And the day after that. And the day after that.” </i> </b><br><br>I felt that the werewolf plot was no longer a priority in this book, at least not as much as it was in the other books. For Sam and Grace, the werewolf issue was about not being able to escape their circumstances. For Cole, it’s his escape from his human self. For Isabel, the wolf is a reminder of everything she’s lost and everything she hasn’t been able to move past. In fiction, a werewolf is never just a wolf, it’s always a metaphor that reflects the character’s true selves. <br><br>Overall, I am so freaking glad that Maggie wrote this book and gave the readers an ending they could cherish. Sinner is a wonderful story of redemption and love, and how we need to move past what we once were to become who we really are.<br><br>My casting:<br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/sinncast.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404962974i/10314243.png" alt=" photo sinncast.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="2629719239072345290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer13894481723295675339"><b> 4 Stars!! </b><br/>🌟🌟🌟🌟<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“It was the first time I'd really realized I'd lost my soul and that the beauty of not having a soul was that you couldn't seem to care that you no longer had one.” </i>
</b><br/><br/>Another series in the books! I love Maggie Stiefvater :P Her writing is so simple, yet complex and the depth expressed in this book was excellent!!<br/><br/>Sinner, is the last book in The Wolves of Mercy Falls series. Its all about my two favorite characters- Isabel and Cole. I could relate to them so much more than Grace a</span>
  <span id="freeText13894481723295675339" style="display:none"><b> 4 Stars!! </b><br />🌟🌟🌟🌟<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“It was the first time I'd really realized I'd lost my soul and that the beauty of not having a soul was that you couldn't seem to care that you no longer had one.” </i>
</b><br /><br />Another series in the books! I love Maggie Stiefvater :P Her writing is so simple, yet complex and the depth expressed in this book was excellent!!<br /><br />Sinner, is the last book in The Wolves of Mercy Falls series. Its all about my two favorite characters- Isabel and Cole. I could relate to them so much more than Grace and Sam. They are just more my cup of tea. You know, the dark characters with hella messed up past, YEAH- I feel that! This one was not really like the rest of the series. Its not a stand alone but its just different and I loved it. <br /><br />I like that we get to really see into what makes these characters tick and what they are really struggling with. I really appreciate the way the author wrote about addiction and how it really can grip a person and the struggles that they face- even when sober. It was done extremely well, especially for it being a YA book. I recommend this series as a whole- mainly for these two characters. They brought a realness to the series. Something raw and not fairy-tale perfect. This was an excellent ending!!</span>
